10.1016/j.jmp.2023.102803
Knowledge space theory (KST) is a mathematical theory first proposed by  Doignon and Falmagne (1985, 1988) . It determines students’ cognitive level in different knowledge by analyzing their answers to a series of relevant questions at different levels. Based on theories such as pedagogy and psychology, KST has established a set of mathematical theories to reflect the laws of education, which provides an effective scientific method for educational evaluation. KST is also a theory to test students’ knowledge states and construct their knowledge structures.

In the early stage of KST, knowledge spaces were at the focus of their development. It is pretty reasonable to assume that two students interacting for a while will eventually merge their initial state of knowledge into a single state which is the union of the two.  Doignon and Falmagne (1985)  generalized Birkhoff’s Theorem ( Birkhoff, 1937 ) and showed that (granular) knowledge spaces are in a one-to-one correspondence with surmise systems. AND/OR graphs of artificial intelligence ( Nilsson, 1971 ) can be used to intuitively understand the relationship between items and foundations in a surmise system.  Koppen (1998)  introduced additional conditions on surmise functions and investigated their consequences for the corresponding spaces (especially for well-graded knowledge spaces).  Ge and Lin (2021)  further studied attribution functions (esp. surmise functions) from the perspective of discriminativeness and resolubility.  Shen et al. (2021)  introduced the completeness (completion) of attribution functions that were in a one-to-one correspondence to knowledge spaces.

Classic KST assumes that an individual’s answer to an item is true or false. This dichotomous representation has limitations in the evaluation of knowledge and learning. To address this limitation,  Schrepp (1997)  generalized the main concepts of KST to problems with more than two answers, using linear ordered sets to evaluate the quality of solutions.  Bartl and Belohlavek (2011)  discussed the theory of knowledge spaces with graded knowledge states.  Stefanutti et al. (2020)  introduced a new formulation of the polytomous KST, assuming that the response levels form a complete lattice.  Heller (2021)  extended the quasi-ordinal knowledge space to the polytomous case and incorporated the methods of Schrepp and Stefanutti et al. into his generalization structure.  Wang et al. (2022a)  explored a specific polytomous knowledge structure: CD-polytomous knowledge space, and it can be regarded as the extension of knowledge space in the polytomous case. Other notes on polytomous generalization can be referred to  Wang et al. (2022b) .

Heller (2021)  introduced the extended polytomous knowledge structure, the element of which is the extended polytomous knowledge state. Each extended polytomous state represents all polytomous items that a subject can solve. This paper presents an extended surmise system, and it takes advantage of the characteristics of the extended polytomous knowledge structure and then defines the clause for each polytomous item. Naturally, it is a generalization of Heller’s concepts of (pre-)precedence relations, allowing more than one possible learning foundation for a polytomous item. This paper also shows the relationship between the extended surmise systems and the CD-polytomous knowledge spaces. In addition,  Wang et al. (2022a)  proposed the concept of a polytomous surmise system. Although the structures generated by the two surmise systems may be the same, the extended surmise system in this paper is different from that of Wang et al. who consider the polytomous surmise system from the perspective of polytomous knowledge structure. The article is structured as follows: Section  2  provides relevant concepts of KST. Section  3  proposes the extended surmise system and Galois connection, and Section  4  gives some notes on the polytomous surmise systems and the (pre-)precedence relations. A final discussion is in Section  5 .

By virtue of these concepts and classical theory derived from KST, all the knowledge spaces in  
                         A 
                       and all the surmise functions in  
                         B 
                       are closed elements under the Galois connection, and a one-to-one correspondence between the two sets of closed elements can be obtained.

The concepts introduced so far belong to classical KST. Next, the concepts related to polytomous KST will be presented. Let  
                         Q 
                       be a finite set of items and  
                         V 
                       a finite set of response values representing the levels of mastery for the subjects to each item  
                         q 
                       in  
                         Q 
                      . Moreover, we assume that the response levels in  
                         V 
                       form a lattice. That is a partially ordered set such that for any pair  
                         
                            { 
                            u 
                            , 
                            v 
                            } 
                         
                       in  
                         V 
                      , the supremum (or least upper bound) and infimum (or greatest lower bound) of that pair exist. We use the join and meet of  
                         
                            { 
                            u 
                            , 
                            v 
                            } 
                         
                       (i.e.,  
                         
                            u 
                            ∨ 
                            v 
                         
                       and  
                         
                            u 
                            ∧ 
                            v 
                         
                      ) instead of the supremum and infimum of  
                         
                            { 
                            u 
                            , 
                            v 
                            } 
                         
                       (abbr.  
                         
                            sup 
                            
                               { 
                               u 
                               , 
                               v 
                               } 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            inf 
                            
                               { 
                               u 
                               , 
                               v 
                               } 
                            
                         
                      ).

A finite lattice is a complete lattice, which means that joins and meets exist for any subset  
                         W 
                       of  
                         V 
                      . In that case, we write  
                         
                            ⋁ 
                            W 
                         
                       and  
                         
                            ⋀ 
                            W 
                         
                       for the join and meet of  
                         W 
                      . The notations  
                         ⊤ 
                       and  
                         ⊥ 
                       represent the top element ( 
                         
                            ⋁ 
                            V 
                         
                      ) and bottom element ( 
                         
                            ⋀ 
                            V 
                         
                      ) of  
                         V 
                      , respectively (see ( Davey & Priestley, 2002 ), for details on the lattice and complete lattice). It is assumed throughout this paper that  
                         Q 
                       and  
                         V 
                       are finite and non-empty sets and that  
                         
                            ( 
                            V 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                       is a lattice.

Notice that  Schrepp (1997)  and  Stefanutti et al. (2020)  also considered the notions of polytomous knowledge structure. However, their polytomous structures are just non-empty subsets of  
                         
                            
                               V

                                  q

                            ×

                            ×

                               ⊤ 
                               } 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            Q 
                            × 
                            
                               { 
                               ⊥ 
                               } 
                            
                         
                       and does not require the covering property.

Because there is a certain relationship between polytomous items, the corresponding structure may be a weak polytomous knowledge structure. That is, an individual does not necessarily need to master each polytomous item from  
                         
                            Q 
                            × 
                            V 
                         
                       in order to reach the polytomous state  
                         
                            Q 
                            × 
                            
                               { 
                               ⊤ 
                               } 
                            
                         
                       (see Section  4  for a specific example). In addition, we cannot think of  Definition 5  as a polytomous extension of the classical partial knowledge structure as introduced in  Falmagne and Doignon (2011) . Because when we consider confining the response categories to a linearly ordered set  
                         
                            { 
                            0 
                            , 
                            1 
                            } 
                         
                      , the structure satisfying  Definition 5  at this point is a dichotomous knowledge structure, not a partial one.

The downset operator

                                     v

                                     K

                                        p

                                     }

                                        p

Definition 6

                                  L 
                                  ∈ 
                                  K

                                           p

                                        L

                                        p 
                                        ∈ 
                                        Q 
                                        .

                               K

                                  K

                                  Q 
                               
                            
                            , 
                            ⊑ 
                            ) 
                         
                       is a lattice, where all joins and meets are defined item-wise. However, for a proper subset

                            ⊔ 
                            011 
                            = 
                            112 
                         
                       means that the join is not defined item-wise.

Heller (2021)  provided a special kind of operation for the join by only considering the  component-directed  subsets of the structure.

                         ( Davey & Priestley, 2002 ) Let

                                  w

                                  u 
                               
                            .

Definition 9

This section puts forward an extended surmise system and shows its corresponding conclusions. First, let us consider the following example. Notice that  
                         
                            
                               
                                  q 
                               
                               
                                  v 
                               
                            
                            ∈ 
                            
                               
                                  K 
                               
                               
                                  ∗ 
                               
                            
                         
                       can be interpreted to mean that the individual has mastered the item  
                         q 
                       at least to the degree  
                         v 
                      . Therefore, when  
                         
                            K 
                            
                               ( 
                               q 
                               ) 
                            
                            = 
                            w 
                         
                       and  
                         
                            v 
                            ≤ 
                            w 
                         
                      , it implies that the individual in the state  
                         K 
                       has mastered the polytomous item  
                         
                            
                               q 
                            
                            
                               v 
                            
                         
                      .

Considering the characteristics of polytomous knowledge structure, that is, every

                            where all component-directed joins are defined item-wise, and the collection of all extended surmise functions on

                            .

                            where all component-directed joins are defined item-wise, and the collection of all extended surmise functions on

                            .

Moreover, the triple  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  V 
                                  , 
                                  δ 
                                  ) 
                               
                             is called a  polytomous surmise system .

For a polytomous knowledge structure, the polytomous surmise function can be obtained in the following ways. Furthermore, if the polytomous knowledge structure is a CD-polytomous knowledge space, then it corresponds to a unique polytomous surmise function.

Through  Theorems 3 and 4 , it is not difficult to draw the following conclusions.

Theorem 5 
                         
                            There is a one-to-one correspondence between the polytomous surmise functions on  
                            
                               
                                  Q 
                                  × 
                                  V 
                               
                            
                            , and the normal extended surmise functions on  
                            
                               
                                  Q 
                                  × 
                                  V 
                               
                            
                            .

There is a one-to-one correspondence between the polytomous surmise functions on  
                            
                               
                                  Q 
                                  × 
                                  V 
                               
                            
                            , and the normal extended surmise functions on  
                            
                               
                                  Q 
                                  × 
                                  V 
                               
                            
                            .

Although  Theorem 5  establishes a one-to-one correspondence between two types of surmise systems, both types can be generated from the same knowledge structure. However, this does not mean that the two types of surmise systems are identical.  Examples 4 and 5  illustrate the case. The normal extended surmise function  
                         
                            
                               σ 
                            
                            
                               K 
                            
                         
                       and polytomous surmise function  
                         
                            
                               δ 
                            
                            
                               K 
                            
                         
                       may differ for the same polytomous knowledge structure  
                         K 
                      —specifically,  
                         
                            
                               
                                  σ 
                               
                               
                                  K 
                               
                            
                            
                               ( 
                               
                                  
                                     c 
                                  
                                  
                                     1 
                                  
                               
                               ) 
                            
                            = 
                            
                               { 
                               111 
                               , 
                               022 
                               , 
                               202 
                               } 
                            
                         
                       in  Example 4  and  
                         
                            
                               
                                  δ 
                               
                               
                                  K 
                               
                            
                            
                               ( 
                               
                                  
                                     c 
                                  
                                  
                                     1 
                                  
                               
                               ) 
                            
                            = 
                            
                               { 
                               111 
                               } 
                            
                         
                       in  Example 5 . The polytomous surmise system emphasizes that if  
                         C 
                       is a clause for the polytomous item  
                         
                            
                               c 
                            
                            
                               1 
                            
                         
                      , then its response value at  
                         c 
                       must be precisely equal to  
                         1 
                      . So the clauses all come from the set  
                         
                            
                               
                                  K 
                               
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        c 
                                     
                                     
                                        1 
                                     
                                  
                               
                            
                            = 
                            
                               { 
                               K 
                               ∈ 
                               K 
                               : 
                               K 
                               
                                  ( 
                                  c 
                                  ) 
                               
                               = 
                               1 
                               } 
                            
                         
                      . In the case of the normal extended surmise system, for any clause  
                         C 
                       for  
                         
                            
                               c 
                            
                            
                               1 
                            
                         
                      ,  
                         
                            C 
                            
                               ( 
                               c

                       could be equal to or greater than  
                         1 
                      . That is why  
                         
                            022 
                         
                       and

                       are clauses for  
                         
                            
                               σ 
                            
                            
                               K 
                            
                         
                       at  
                         
                            
                               c

                      .

Heller treated each  
                         
                            
                               
                                  p 
                               
                               
                                  v 
                               
                            
                            ∈ 
                            Q 
                            × 
                            V 
                         
                       as a virtual item and provided the binary relation  
                         ≼ 
                       on  
                         
                            Q 
                            × 
                            V 
                         
                      
 ( Heller, 2021 ). That is, for

                                  w 
                               
                            
                         
                       can be interpreted as if an individual responds at least with

                       to item

                      , then the individual responds at least with  
                         v 
                       to item

                      . Furthermore, he proposed the notions of (pre-)precedence relations on

                            × 
                            V

                                     , 
                                     b 
                                     } 
                                  
                               
                             and  
                               
                                  V 
                                  = 
                                  
                                     { 
                                     0 
                                     , 
                                     1 
                                     , 
                                     2 
                                     } 
                                  
                               
                             with the numerical relation “less than or equal” on  
                               V 
                            . Given the following precedence relations  
                               ≼ 
                             on  
                               
                                  Q 
                                  × 
                                  V 
                               
                            : (1) the trivial ones, that is,  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        q 
                                     
                                     
                                        0 
                                     
                                  
                                  ≼ 
                                  
                                     
                                        q 
                                     
                                     
                                        1 
                                     
                                  
                                  ≼ 
                                  
                                     
                                        q 
                                     
                                     
                                        2 
                                     
                                  
                               
                            , where item  
                               q 
                             is  
                               a 
                             or  
                               b 
                            ; (2) the nontrivial one,  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        a 
                                     
                                     
                                        2 
                                     
                                  
                                  ≼ 
                                  
                                     
                                        b 
                                     
                                     
                                        2 
                                     
                                  
                               
                            . It means that if an individual has mastered  
                               
                                  
                                     b 
                                  
                                  
                                     2 
                                  
                               
                            , he must also have grasped  
                               
                                  
                                     a 
                                  
                                  
                                     2 
                                  
                               
                            . The polytomous knowledge structure corresponding to this precedence relation  
                               ≼ 
                             is as follows:  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                        = 
                                        
                                           { 
                                           00 
                                           , 
                                           01 
                                           , 
                                           10 
                                           , 
                                           11 
                                           , 
                                           20 
                                           , 
                                           21 
                                           , 
                                           22 
                                           } 
                                        
                                        . 
                                     
                                  
                               
                            A novice is assumed to know nothing at all at the beginning, which means that his polytomous state is  
                               
                                  00 
                               
                            . After a period of effective learning, he achieves the polytomous state  
                               
                                  22 
                               
                            . In this learning process, he may choose a practical way: to learn  
                               
                                  
                                     b 
                                  
                                  
                                     1 
                                  
                               
                             first and then  
                               
                                  
                                     b 
                                  
                                  
                                     2 
                                  
                               
                            . If he is capable of solving item  
                               b 
                             at degree 1, then a transition between state  
                               
                                  00 
                               
                             to  
                               
                                  01 
                               
                             occurs. On that basis, he moves on to  
                               
                                  
                                     b 
                                  
                                  
                                     2 
                                  
                               
                            , and his polytomous state further transitions from  
                               
                                  01 
                               
                             to  
                               
                                  22 
                               
                            . The polytomous states he experiences are the collection  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        1 
                                     
                                  
                                  = 
                                  
                                     { 
                                     00 
                                     , 
                                     01 
                                     , 
                                     22 
                                     } 
                                  
                               
                            . Obviously,  
                               
                                  
                                     K 
                                  
                                  
                                     1 
                                  
                               
                             is a weak polytomous knowledge structure, indicating that the subject may not necessarily master  
                               
                                  
                                     a 
                                  
                                  
                                     1 
                                  
                               
                             in his learning process.

Now we provide a weaker concept of extended surmise function, namely, the  extended pre-surmise function . It is a concept derived from  Definition 11  by removing its Condition (ii). The collection of all extended pre-surmise functions on  
                         
                            Q 
                            × 
                            V 
                         
                       encompasses the collection of all pre-precedence relations on  
                         
                            Q 
                            × 
                            V 
                         
                      .

Proof 
                         Let  
                               σ 
                             be an extended pre-surmise function on  
                               
                                  Q 
                                  × 
                                  V 
                               
                            . Using a proof similar to  Lemma 2 , we can see that  
                               
                                  
                                     K 
                                  
                                  
                                     σ 
                                  
                               
                             contains  
                               
                                  Q 
                                  × 
                                  
                                     { 
                                     ⊤ 
                                     } 
                                  
                               
                            , where all component-directed joins are defined item-wise. Since  
                               
                                  σ 
                                  
                                     ( 
                                     
                                        
                                           q 
                                        
                                        
                                           w 
                                        
                                     
                                     ) 
                                  
                               
                             has only one clause for each  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        q 
                                     
                                     
                                        w 
                                     
                                  
                                  ∈ 
                                  Q 
                                  × 
                                  V 
                               
                            , we can see that  
                               
                                  
                                     K 
                                  
                                  
                                     σ 
                                  
                                  
                                     ∗ 
                                  
                               
                             is closed under the intersection. (For any  
                               
                                  
                                     K 
                                  
                                  
                                     1 
                                  
                                  
                                     ∗ 
                                  
                               
                            ,  
                               
                                  
                                     K 
                                  
                                  
                                     2 
                                  
                                  
                                     ∗ 
                                  
                               
                             in  
                               
                                  
                                     K 
                                  
                                  
                                     σ 
                                  
                                  
                                     ∗ 
                                  
                               
                             and each  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        q 
                                     
                                     
                                        w 
                                     
                                  
                                  ∈ 
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        1 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∗ 
                                     
                                  
                                  ∩ 
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        2 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∗ 
                                     
                                  
                               
                            , we have  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        q 
                                     
                                     
                                        w 
                                     
                                  
                                  ∈ 
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        1 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∗ 
                                     
                                  
                               
                             and  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        q 
                                     
                                     
                                        w 
                                     
                                  
                                  ∈ 
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        2 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∗ 
                                     
                                  
                               
                            . There is only one clause  
                               
                                  C 
                                  ∈ 
                                  σ 
                                  
                                     ( 
                                     
                                        
                                           q 
                                        
                                        
                                           w 
                                        
                                     
                                     ) 
                                  
                               
                             such that  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        C 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∗ 
                                     
                                  
                                  ⊆ 
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        1 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∗ 
                                     
                                  
                               
                             and  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        C 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∗ 
                                     
                                  
                                  ⊆ 
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        2 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∗ 
                                     
                                  
                               
                            , i.e.,  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        C 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∗ 
                                     
                                  
                                  ⊆ 
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        1 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∗

Heller (2021)  introduced the concept of polytomous knowledge structure, which provides a more rigorous framework compared to the corresponding concepts proposed by  Schrepp (1997)  and  Stefanutti et al. (2020) . In Heller’s definition, polytomous knowledge structures are required to include top and bottom elements, and each polytomous item is associated with a state within the polytomous knowledge structure. These specific requirements may not be explicitly mentioned in the literature of  Schrepp (1997)  and  Stefanutti et al. (2020) . In this paper, we present a novel exploration of polytomous knowledge structure that offers a complementary perspective and contributes as an addition to the existing approaches within the field of polytomous knowledge structure theory. Our focus is on a less restrictive form of polytomous knowledge structure, which serves as an extension of the traditional dichotomous knowledge structure, as outlined in  Definition 5 . In addition, in the actual learning process, a structure does not necessarily contain every element of  
                         
                            Q 
                            × 
                            V 
                         
                      .

When looking for the corresponding surmise system for a weak polytomous knowledge structure, we find that the polytomous surmise system proposed by  Wang et al. (2022a)  is not necessarily suitable for the requirements of this paper. The reason is that  Wang et al. (2022a)  have strict requirements for the clauses. That is, for any element  
                         C 
                       in the set of clauses for  
                         
                            
                               q 
                            
                            
                               v 
                            
                         
                      , the response value of  
                         C 
                       at item  
                         q 
                       must be exactly equal to  
                         v 
                      . However, a weak polytomous knowledge structure may not contain the  
                         
                            
                               q 
                            
                            
                               v 
                            
                         
                       mentioned above, so there is no way to define the clauses of the polytomous items in the way of  Wang et al. (2022a) . In polytomous KST, it is reasonable to believe that the way individuals master each  
                         
                            
                               q 
                            
                            
                               v 
                            
                         
                       is not unique but more flexible. So we present the extended surmise system as introduced in  Definition 11 . In line with classical KST ideas, we can establish Galois connections between weak polytomous knowledge structures and extended attribution functions, and so on. Then,  Theorems 2 and 3 , and  Corollary 1 , present several one-to-one correspondences between the various collections.

If the “polytomous surmise systems”, including both the one proposed by  Wang et al. (2022a)  and the normal extended surmise system presented in this paper, are defined on the same polytomous knowledge structure  
                         K 
                      , they are considered equivalent (see  Theorem 5  for details). Both surmise systems generate the same polytomous structures, while the component-directed joins are defined item-wise. In addition, it is easy to see the connection between the extended polytomous surmise systems and Heller’s precedence relations. In particular, the normal extended surmise systems can be viewed as a generalization of the precedence relations, and the extended pre-surmise systems generalize the pre-precedence relations. The main reason is that, for the (pre-)precedence relations, any polytomous item has a unique clause, while for the extended surmise systems there may be multiple clauses. Therefore,  Theorem 7  is true whenever the number of clauses for each polytomous item is 1.

The next step is to show the relationship between the three new surmise functions introduced in this article. From their definition, the conditions required by the normal extended surmise function are the most demanding. By contrast, those required by the extended surmise function are less stringent. The extended pre-surmise function requires fewer conditions than the previous two. Therefore, a normal extended surmise function must be an extended surmise function, and an extended surmise function is also an extended pre-surmise function—however, none of these inclusions holds the other way around.

As for the generation of the surmise system in polytomous KST, there have been several theories ( Ge, 2022; Schrepp, 1997; Stefanutti et al., 2020; Wang et al., 2022a, 2022b ) that are more or less related to each other. The task at hand is to integrate these existing theories into a unified framework and explore the potential emergence of novel polytomous surmise systems in the future. This direction may open up promising avenues for future research in the field of polytomous knowledge structure theory.
